The talk will express strong opinions on establishing a Manchurian and Mongolian national policy and promoting the resolution of outstanding issues.

The British House of Commons Passes Vote of Confidence in the National Government by a Margin of Fifty-Nine Votes 71

The Prime Minister Elaborates on the Handling of the Crisis

▲[Reuters, London, 8th] Parliament reconvened today, and the nation's attention was focused here. Parliament adjourned at the end of July and was originally scheduled to reconvene on October 22nd. However, due to the government's proposals to reduce government spending and increase taxes in order to restore the nation's fiscal balance, which urgently needed to be passed and implemented, Parliament convened a special session today. Former Labour Party leader Prime Minister MacDonald appeared in the House of Commons today, allied with the leaders of the Conservative and Liberal parties, who had previously been in opposition. As for the Labour Party members who had previously supported MacDonald, they were all seated in the opposition seats, with only a dozen or so remaining loyal to their former leader. After the King's Speech was read, the Prime Minister moved that the House of Commons Committee on Finance be established on Thursday to receive Chancellor of the Exchequer Snowden's special supplementary budget. The Prime Minister then spoke, saying that the current emergency situation was an extraordinary event in politics and a test of democratic government. Democratic government often cannot save itself from sudden danger. It is gratifying to see how the people have united to deal with the emergency situation, he said. The Prime Minister continued to speak about the government's handling of the tense situation, saying that on August 8th, the Bank of England's gold reserves were threatened by a large number of withdrawals, indicating that a serious situation was about to occur. With the situation pressing, a temporary loan was secured to prevent a sharp decline in the pound. If no measures had been taken at that time, a real panic would have broken out, and the pound would not only have been slightly devalued but would have plummeted to zero. Subsequently, the storm continued unabated, and the government had to act quickly to consolidate its defenses. The situation was caused by various reasons from home and abroad. It should not be mistaken as due to a possible lack of public savings but was actually due to a wavering of confidence. Lack of confidence is extremely harmful, and our complex credit structure would be significantly affected. We were forced by the situation to borrow money, and borrowing must balance the budget and place unemployment finance on a solid financial foundation. Some say that the establishment of the National Government was based on external pressure from the international financial community. In reality, bankers and financiers, no matter how selfish, would not want to devise political methods to bankrupt themselves. He can declare unequivocally that all negotiations were conducted by the Chancellor of the Exchequer and the Prime Minister with the consent of the government. The banks never interfered in political proposals during the negotiations. They only stated their professional opinions and predicted the impact of political proposals on borrowing. He is willing to work with anyone who acknowledges that no external authority can control national politics (government supporters cheer). This principle applies not only to finance but also to any institution (referring to trade unions). The banks' contact with the government was always limited to their legitimate banking business, he said. The Prime Minister praised the goodwill expressed by American and French bankers and said that important negotiations on reparations and debt repayment would take place soon. Therefore, he hoped that the opposition would speak cautiously and not attack foreigners because of domestic affairs, he said. A Labour Party member shouted, "Is the Prime Minister himself affected by the spending cuts?" MacDonald replied, "I will take a cut of £1,000 per year myself." After the Prime Minister's speech, which lasted an hour, opposition leader Henderson rose and said that there were two types of cuts that the Labour Party could not accept: one was the expenditure on social programs, and the other was unemployment benefits. The entire previous Labour cabinet had agreed to save £56 million, but MacDonald and Snowden, after consulting with the leaders of the Conservative and Liberal parties, proposed to save another £30 million, most of which would have to come from the unemployed, he said. The current Home Secretary, Liberal Samuel, rose to vehemently deny Henderson's claims on behalf of the Conservative and Liberal parties. Henderson continued, saying that he had no criticism of the banks and that his trust in the relationship between Britain, France, and the United States led him to the conclusion that France and the United States would never dare to allow British credit to collapse for their own benefit, he said. The current Lord President of the Council, Baldwin, rose and said that the financial problem had become the most urgent matter. No matter how unpleasant the remedy, no one has the right to refuse it. Therefore, the Conservative Party has no other choice but to agree to give MacDonald the assistance it can. Until the government's work is completed, the Conservative Party will do its best to help. If the opposition's attitude causes other countries to misunderstand that a large part of the British people do not understand the seriousness of their position and are unwilling to deal with their current difficulties, then the opposition bears a heavy responsibility and must examine itself. If Britain's international credit collapses, there will be an unprecedented disaster, not only affecting Britain but also the entire human race, he said. Mosley, who had previously left the Labour Party to form a new party, stated his position today, saying that he hoped the government could achieve its goals, but he felt that the proposed plan was not sufficient. He advocated implementing a vigorous industrial policy and said that it would be useless to balance the budget based on existing revenues. Churchill, who had previously disagreed with Conservative Party leaders on Indian policy, said that all imported goods must be taxed, otherwise, it would be impossible to restore Britain's finances and industrial status. Churchill was originally a free trader, and his remarks surprised those who heard them. He probably wanted to cater to the psychology of the protectionists in the Conservative Party and hope to get their support in future political activities. After speeches from various sides, the assembly voted and passed the vote of confidence by 309 votes to 250. When the result was announced, there was a great cheer. The National Government's first day in the House of Commons ended in a victory. At the same time, there was also a discussion in the House of Lords, but the scope was smaller, and the number of opposition members was not large enough to resist the majority. After the Lord Chancellor read the King's Speech, the new Foreign Secretary, Sir Reading, spoke on behalf of the government, outlining the causes of the current financial crisis and the changes in the cabinet. He concluded by saying that the new government will resolutely strive to restore financial stability and is sure to get the support of the people. Opposition leader Passfield rose and said that the reduction of unemployment benefits was the most unsatisfactory thing. Therefore, the opposition completely distrusts the new government. Spending cuts are necessary, but the opposition believes that spending cuts should be implemented according to the ability to pay, he said. The House of Lords then adjourned until September 17th.

Official Telegram

To the Shen Bao Newspaper Office in Nanjing, Upon reading your esteemed newspaper's report on the 8th regarding the Nanjing telegram on the 7th, which stated that Chairman Chiang summoned Acting President Shao to inquire about the situation in the Legislative Yuan, this is not factual. We hope you will make a correction. [Signed] Secretariat of the Legislative Yuan [seal]

Page 11

Official Telegram Two

To all newspaper offices in Beiping, This year, the central and southern provinces have experienced unprecedented floods, a disaster of immense proportions rarely seen in ancient times. We have received numerous letters and telegrams from various parties, fully understanding the tragic situation. Our hearts ache for the disaster victims, and we are deeply concerned. It is only through the collective effort of all that we can provide relief. Therefore, we have established the "Flood Relief Association of Various Provinces" at our Deputy Commander's Headquarters, with branches in the governments of Hebei, Shanxi, Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Jehol, Chahar, and Suiyuan provinces, the special municipalities of Harbin and Weihaiwei, and the municipal governments of Beiping, Tianjin, and Qingdao. Zhang Xueliang will serve concurrently as the president of the association, and the governors and mayors of each province and municipality will serve as vice presidents. We are organizing and establishing these associations immediately and will work diligently to solicit donations of money and grain and send them to the Central Flood Relief Committee for distribution to the disaster areas, hoping to make a small contribution and alleviate the disaster. With reconstruction needed and anxiety weighing heavily on us, we hereby report this situation for your consideration. [Signed] Zhang Xueliang [seal]

To all newspaper offices in Nanchang, Unfortunately, Jiangxi Province has been afflicted by both natural disasters and man-made calamities. The scourge of the communists has not been eliminated, and floods have been reported repeatedly. Since the beginning of summer, mountain torrents have erupted, turning houses into ruins and fields into nothingness. People and animals have been swept away, and death is widespread, turning many areas into marshes. This time, the Yangtze River flood has also affected northern Jiangxi, and transportation to Nanxun is still mostly obstructed. According to a survey conducted by our province's disaster relief commissioners, the flooded area covers more than 3,700 square miles, with losses estimated at more than 100 million yuan. The disaster area is vast, and the disaster is extraordinarily severe. Autumn is approaching, and we do not know how we will survive. Thinking of this, our anxiety deepens. We humbly request the officials of the party and government to quickly allocate funds for relief so that the dying people of Jiangxi can recover and flourish. We also appeal to all charitable people to act with compassion, providing aid to the hungry and drowning. Whether by donating generously or soliciting donations, the more the better, so that all disaster victims can benefit. Our association will express its gratitude on behalf of the people. With sadness in our telegram, we humbly beg for your understanding and consideration. [Signed] Jiangxi Provincial Association of All Trades

The Central Government Holds a Memorial for Dr. Sun Yat-sen's First Uprising 75

Shao Yuanchong Reports on the Significance and Lessons of the Uprising

The Central Party Headquarters held a memorial meeting for Dr. Sun Yat-sen's First Uprising at 8:00 AM on the 9th. Present were Chiang Kai-shek, Yu Youren, Ding Weifen, Shao Yuanchong, Zhu Peide, En Kemaguoguo, Fang Juehui, Zhang Renjie, Zeng Yangfu, Wu Jingheng, Wang Zhengting, Zhu Jiahua, Wang Boqun, Lu Dipin, Wang Bailing, Zhang Daofan, Chen Lifu, Yi Peiji, Niu Yongjian, and over 600 other staff and guests. After the opening ceremony led by Chairman Yu Youren, Shao Yuanchong reported on the significance and lessons of the First Uprising, stating that Dr. Sun Yat-sen's First Uprising was now thirty-seven years ago. After the Taiping Rebellion at the end of the Qing Dynasty, imperialism gradually exerted its political and economic aggression, and the country's situation became perilous. Dr. Sun Yat-sen knew that revolution was the only way to save the country. He opened hospitals and pharmacies in Guangdong and Hong Kong as revolutionary organs and used the Agricultural Society as a base for propaganda. There were contacts with the defense battalions and the navy. He decided to take advantage of the Double Ninth Festival by using tomb sweeping as a pretext to avoid the attention of the Manchus and launch the uprising. Unexpectedly, Zhu Qi revealed the secret to his brother, who, fearing the extermination of his family, informed the authorities. On the 9th, the Manchu government cracked down on several revolutionary organs. Dr. Sun Yat-sen had gone to Macau and then to Hong Kong. Zhu Gui, Quan Cheng, Kui Guang, and others were martyred. This was truly the beginning of the Three Principles of the People's revolutionary movement. After many uprisings, success was finally achieved. Therefore, its significance is very significant. In general, those who bear the responsibility of creation face very difficult circumstances. Those who are prescient and enlightened must have great courage to bear the responsibility of creation. Historically, the greatest thing is the creative enterprise. Dr. Sun Yat-sen had a far-sighted vision and judged that the situation in China at the end of the Qing Dynasty could not be saved without a revolution of ideology. Therefore, there was the great creation. The failure of the First Uprising was not because the strength was not equal to the Manchus but because Zhu Qi's brother informed the authorities, and it was first destroyed from within. Things must rot before worms appear. If an organization is not unified internally and is not tightly organized, it can never succeed. Today's China must rely on the Kuomintang to complete the responsibility of the revolution. However, it must not break down from within. Moreover, the severity of the national flood this time is unprecedented in history. Not only members of our party but also the entire nation should work together to bear the responsibility of saving the country from danger. The bandits are being gradually wiped out, and if there are no other forces to undermine us, they will certainly be wiped out in the shortest time. At the same time, international imperialists are exerting various severe pressures on us. Under these circumstances, we should abandon our prejudices and lead the nation as a whole, and anyone with a conscience should abandon their prejudices and work together with all party comrades and the people of the country to save the country and overcome the current difficulties, and so on. The meeting adjourned after Shao's report.

Guangdong and Guangxi Armies Invade Hunan Again 76

Various Leaders Decide on a Plan to Deal with the Situation

Liu Jianxu Immediately Goes to Hengzhou to Deploy Defenses

Changsha Correspondence, The rumors of the Guangdong and Guangxi armies invading Hunan have been circulating for a long time. In early August, Gui Jun's (Guangxi Army) Tan Lianfang's division crossed the Huangsha River and advanced to Fangzhu Village, 30 li from Yongzhou. Han Caifeng's unit arrived at Longhuguan, and part of Zhang Fakui's unit also arrived at Yongming. Yue Jun's (Guangdong Army) Li Yangjing's unit then attempted to spy on Xuanzhang from Pingshi. At that time, He Jian was deploying troops to deal with the situation when suddenly the Zhang armies of Guangdong and Guangxi simultaneously withdrew on their own initiative. In the past three or four days, there have been secondary rumors of the Guangdong and Guangxi armies invading Hunan. The authorities initially thought it was still a false alarm, so they did not pay much attention. Unexpectedly, according to reports from southern Hunan, the Guangdong and Guangxi armies are advancing north in three routes: (1) Yue Jun's Li Yangjing and Yu Hanmou units enter Hunan from Pingshi; (2) Gui Jun, led by Bai Chongxi, commands the 47th and 4th Armies and is scheduled to mobilize into Hunan on September 4th; (3) Zhang Fakui's unit enters Hunan from Longhuguan. At this time, He Jian had gone to various counties to inspect the disaster. Cao Dianqiu, the acting chairman of the provincial government, reported the situation at noon and immediately telegraphed He Jian, asking him to return to the province as soon as possible to plan military affairs. He also sent a telegram to Commander-in-Chief Chiang, asking him to quickly send more troops to Hunan to help defend the province. On the evening of the 2nd, a meeting was held with the provincial military and political leaders to discuss defense and dispatched the First Hunan Aviation Squadron to Heng on the morning of the 3rd to receive dispatch and assistance from Army Commander Liu and Division Commander Tao. After the discussion, Liu Jianxu left the province for Hengzhou on the 3rd. At 3:00 PM, he arrived safely in Hengzhou and sent a radio message reporting that the defenses of Hengzhou were solid and that the Guangdong and Guangxi armies had not yet advanced. He Jian also telegraphed from Changde, stating that he would return to the province on the 5th. He had instructed the generals in the Hengbao area to hold their positions and await orders and not to attack for the time being. On the evening of the 3rd, Commander-in-Chief Chiang also replied to Hunan, stating that he had dispatched the Central Army to Hunan to help defend the province immediately. Given this situation, a war in southern Hunan may break out. However, as of the evening of the 3rd, there were no reports of the Guangdong, Guangxi, or Zhang units arriving at the Hunan border. In order to prevent reactionary propaganda, the General Headquarters has specially appointed Section Chief Song Min as a news censor and has been implementing censorship of military news since the 3rd. (September 4th)

Hubei Disaster Relief Branch Holds Emergency Meeting 77

Decides to Establish Various Specialized Committees

Hankou Correspondence, The Hubei Branch of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee held an emergency meeting of all Chinese and foreign committee members at 2:00 PM on the 5th. He Chengjun also attended the meeting. The meeting was presided over by Fang Benren, chairman of the committee. After the opening ceremony, the following announcements were made: (1) The disaster situation and relief efforts in Hankou (including the three towns of Wuhan). According to the disaster household survey form of the Wuhan Garrison Command, there are 700,000 disaster victims in Hankou, of which more than 276,000 are completely without food, clothing, and shelter and are in urgent need of relief. There are about 100,000 refugees who have fled from other counties and have not yet been included. These disaster victims were originally relieved by the Hubei Flood Relief Association, which was jointly formed by the Hubei Provincial Government, the Wuhan General Chamber of Commerce, and various charitable organizations, as well as various Chinese and foreign groups, individuals, and companies. The Hubei Flood Relief Association spent hundreds of thousands of yuan on relief funds, and the relief funds spent by various Chinese and foreign groups, individuals, and companies were even more numerous. The situation has become difficult for both public and private sectors. The branch should plan in advance how to subsidize the relief efforts in the future so that the lifeline of 270,000 disaster victims will not be interrupted. (2) The approximate number of disaster victims and relief efforts in various counties. After the floods in Hubei, 45 counties reported disasters one after another. The total population of the province is 35 million, with an average of more than 460,000 people per county. Among them, the number of people in need of relief in the disaster area is estimated to be half of the total population of the county, about 230,000 people per county, for a total of more than 10 million disaster victims. The Hubei Provincial Government has sent personnel to investigate and has telegraphed the county magistrates of each county to provide shelter and relief locally. However, the ground in each county is a vast expanse of water, and business has stopped. Where can relief supplies be obtained? The branch previously proposed to purchase a large amount of rice and distribute it according to the severity of the disaster in each county. At the same time, it telegraphed the Shanghai National Government Flood Relief Committee to quickly raise relief rice and transport it to Hankou, and to seek permission from Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui to temporarily relax the rice ban in order to raise funds for procurement. However, if each person's daily ration is calculated at 10 cents, 1 million yuan in national currency is needed, and if it is calculated at 5 cents, 500,000 yuan in foreign currency is needed. Other matters, such as the shelter, clothing, and epidemic prevention of disaster victims, should also be organized immediately, otherwise, millions of disaster victims will be allowed to die without being rescued, which would not be the most unfortunate thing for mankind in the world. The above points are all based on the branch's thorough investigation and statistics. We hope that everyone will express their opinions and do their best to show human compassion and relieve the disaster victims from their imminent doom. This is not only the blessing of Hubei but also the honor of our branch. Next, Chairman Fang Benren reported: (1) The US Consul General handed over US$100,000 donated by the American Red Cross for flood relief, equivalent to more than 457,700 yuan in national currency. (2) The Hubei Provincial Government handed over a telegram from Chairman Liu of Henan, stating that 10,000 reed mats have been purchased, and approximately 3,000 yuan are needed to transport them. Please send someone to escort them. (3) The disaster victim household registration forms for Wuhan and various counties have been formulated by the branch and sent to the provincial government for investigation and reporting. After the report, the formal discussion of the proposals began, and the following was decided: (1) A letter was sent to the provincial government requesting that reed sheds be built on Hongshan, Luojia Mountain, and other spacious locations outside the city to shelter refugees and maintain public security. A motion was made to transfer all refugees in the three towns of Wuhan to Hongshan and Luojia Mountain for shelter. (2) Committee Member Yu Zhi proposed that the disaster situation in the province is extremely severe, and all current relief and future rehabilitation affairs are numerous and need to be planned in detail in order to be beneficial and without harm. It is proposed that the branch hire specialized personnel to organize a specialized committee for employment relief (all matters related to relief and employment relief for disaster victims are included), a specialized committee for economy (all matters related to financial circulation, price stabilization, and the preparation and protection of agricultural affairs are included), and other specialized committees to conduct research and formulate specific plans for implementation. (3) Committee Member Huang Jianzhong proposed to establish a disaster victim education committee. It was decided that the above two proposals should be drafted by Committee Member Yu Zhi and Committee Member Huang Jianzhong and submitted to the next meeting for discussion. Committee Member Edward then made a temporary motion requesting that the Shanghai National Government Flood Relief Association be telegraphed to quickly telegraph the United States to raise large amounts of money for relief. It was decided to pass the motion and hand it over to the executive committee for handling. The meeting adjourned at about 5:00 PM. (September 5th)

The Yellow River's Water Level in Shandong Rises Again 78

Jinan Correspondence, The Yellow River in Shandong had temporarily stabilized after the water level receded repeatedly since the end of last month. However, the water level in the upper reaches of Shaanxi Province has risen again, flowing down and causing the Yellow River in Shandong to rise again. It is estimated that the water level in Shaanxi Province rose 2.4 chi on the 3rd and another 1.5 chi on the 4th. The water that rose twice has now flowed to the middle reaches of Shandong. The water level at Luokou rose 1.1 chi yesterday and another 7 cun today (7th). This year, the water level rose to a maximum of 9 zhang 3 chi above sea level and fell to a minimum of 8 zhang 6 chi 3 cun. Now it has risen again, and the water level has reached 8 zhang 9 chi. However, the tributaries of the Yellow River east of Shaanxi Province, the Luo River and the Yi River, have not risen. Except for the Wangfu River in Changqing east of Zhengzhou, there are no more tributaries flowing into the Yellow River. Since the tributaries have not risen, they will not increase the Yellow River's water volume. The last rise in water in Shaanxi Province will also flow through the middle reaches, and the water level is unlikely to rise significantly again. However, hidden water is hot, and the force is above, while autumn water is cold, and the force is below. Scouring the roots of the dikes, the force of autumn water is the fiercest. When the Li Shengcun breach occurred in the fifteenth year of the Republic, the time was already September 20th. Therefore, even though autumn is approaching, optimism about the Yellow River is not warranted. If the upper reaches continue to rise, the three reaches of this province may not be able to avoid dangerous works again. (September 7th)

The Commissioners Dispatched by Supervisor Zhang Report on the Disaster Situation in Xinghua 79

Yangzhou Correspondence, After the breach of the Grand Canal, in addition to dispatching Adjutant Song Bangrong to investigate the disaster and provide relief, Supervisor Zhang Zhijiang also dispatched Guo Bingquan on the 2nd to Xinghua, Yancheng area to conduct on-the-spot investigations of the disaster in order to accurately provide relief and rehabilitation. According to the report from the commissioners back to Yang, it is stated that it is approximately 130 li from Shaobo to Xinghua. The wind was favorable on the day of departure. He arrived at Yangjia Village. The water depth along the way was measured to be 1 zhang 2 chi. The houses were half-collapsed, and there were a few disaster victims either nesting in trees or living in small boats. Floating coffins could be seen drifting about. Three li from Guocun, a strong northwest wind arose, and the boat drifted with the wind to a place with many trees before stopping. The next morning, after traveling for three hours, the original route was found. After passing Liuan, he sailed to Fanchuan, where the water depth was approximately 3 chi and the houses were also half-collapsed. He traveled along the Gaotai border dike, which had been eroded by water into a serrated shape. Five li out, the dike had already been submerged in water. The boat entered the eastern border of Gaoyou, where the water depth in the paddy fields was 1 zhang 3 chi. There was a floating corpse tied to a tree in the forest, with a belly as big as a drum. In the evening, he arrived at Lao Ge Village in Xinghua. He passed through various villages for approximately ten hours and arrived outside the Zhongzheng Gate of the county, where the water depth was approximately 1 zhang 4 chi. Most of the villagers lived in small boats, guarding their former residences. Outside the South Gate of the county, there was a vast wilderness. From the east to Dongtai, from the west to Gaoyou, and from the south to Taixian, there were white waves, endless and boundless. On the morning of the 4th, he changed to a small boat to enter the city. The water outside the city had submerged half of the door, and the eaves of the deeper houses were level with the water. Inside the city, the water depth was 3 or 4 chi, and the entire city was flooded. Only the county government hall was free of water. At 8:00 AM, the county magistrate was ill in bed, and the section chief was also not on duty. Therefore, he went to Liujia Lane to meet Leng Zeng and went to the county government together to see Magistrate Hua, who inquired about the disaster situation. He replied that due to the continuous rain in summer, half of the fields had already been flooded. Since the Shaodi embankment was breached, the four villages had been submerged, and the people were using boats as homes. The southeast was higher, and there were fewer deaths. As for the relief affairs, the funds were exhausted. The county police force of more than 300 people had been in arrears for three months and had no ability to provide relief to the disaster victims. Fortunately, the province provided 5,000 yuan to purchase noodles for district relief. The province will continue to provide 8,000 yuan. The Jiangsu Relief Association will also come here to provide relief and intends to set up a refugee shelter in the county government, but this is only a drop in the bucket. It is hoped that all parties will provide rapid assistance. As for defense, although bandits are stirring, thanks to the strict defense of the police force, the water patrol team, and the local defense regiment, they are still able to coexist peacefully. When asked about the disaster situation in Yancheng, he replied that the telegraph was not working. However, Yancheng is higher, and it is said that the early rice has been harvested. The situation must be better. He then went to the chamber of commerce to meet Chairman Gu Lunan, who said the same as the county magistrate. He also asked about the method of receding water and replied that the most important thing was to block the breach of the canal embankment and open the Ziwu embankment (ie, the Dafeng embankment). The embankment is in Dongtai, 30 li from the East Sea. However, it is heard that Dafeng does not allow it to be opened. He begged to ask the supervisor to find a way. At the time, there was a Supervisory Inspector from the Civil Affairs Department who arrived from Tai County, saying that the disaster situation in Xinghua was the most serious, followed by Gaoyou Shaobo and the eastern part of Yancheng Tai County, and also said that the embankment had been opened on the 1st, but it was heard that it had been closed again. (September 8th)

Chu Minyi Reports on the Northwest Inspection Trip (Continued) 80

▲ Before departing for the Northwest, Minyi also made a statement, saying that the key to going to the Northwest lies in transportation. Therefore, there was a comparison between opening up Xinjiang and Zuo Zongtang's re-establishing Xinjiang in the past. When discussing these issues with various parties in Xinjiang, they all agreed that Minyi's proposition was correct. Now, returning east from Xinjiang, I deeply feel that the Xinjiang issue is still primarily about transportation. The key to transportation lies in efficient tools. Today's efficient transportation tools include automobiles, steamships, airplanes, and airships. However, none of these are suitable for desert areas. Since there are no railways or roads for automobiles in the desert, it is necessary to create transportation tools other than automobiles, steamships, airplanes, and airships. Therefore, upon hearing about the "crawling automobile" as an efficient tool specifically for traversing deserts, those concerned about transportation in the Northwest were greatly inspired and eager to try it out. If this type of equipment can be successful, it would solve a major problem of transportation in China's Northwest, which is of great importance to the national economy and the people's livelihood. The invention of machinery is a public contribution to humanity and the academic world, regardless of whether the inventor is Chinese or foreign. Therefore, when the French want to promote the capabilities of their crawling automobile, we especially hope for its successful crawling. To be honest, Minyi did not forget his mission of academic investigation and party affairs inspection at the time. However, the investigation and inspection were very short. I personally believe that if the crawling is successful and transportation becomes convenient, the Northwest will be accessible. Why have one investigation when you can have multiple? Why have a small number of people inspect when you can have a large number? What I dare to happily report now is that the crawling automobile is indeed an efficient tool for traversing the desert. China's Northwest transportation will surely usher in a new era because of this efficient tool. Therefore, this Sino-French cooperation can be said to be a failure, but the trial use of the crawling automobile for the development of Xinjiang must be said to be a success. The French side encountered many setbacks and could not meet as scheduled with the east and west teams, which can be said to be a failure. However, the academic investigation and party affairs inspection of the Chinese side must be said to be a success. Therefore, when Minyi saw that Northwest transportation could be solved and that the development of Xinjiang was promising, he felt boundless hope and joy when thinking about the future. He forgot the physical hardships he had suffered. He also forgot the temporary misunderstandings caused by delayed letters and telegrams. Some people deliberately provoked conflicts along the way, not only damaging the relationship between the Chinese and French teams, causing suspicion and resentment, and leading to quarrels and even fights. Even among the Chinese team members, this was the case. Hao Jun's beating and Bu An's throwing punches were nothing more than puppets of these instigators. Although Minyi felt unhappy at times, he believed that the truth would eventually come out. This kind of pain was also forgotten due to the idea that the Northwest could be crawled through and the development of Xinjiang was promising.

▲ There are three major trunk roads in the Northwest transportation routes. Minyi believes that the government should pay close attention and complete these three major trunk roads in the shortest possible time. Otherwise, the Northwest transportation and the development of Xinjiang are hopeless, and Mongolia and Xinjiang will inevitably fall into the hands of foreign powers. These three major trunk roads are: (1) Guihua via the Mongolian desert directly to Guchengzi, which is the camel road currently taken, requiring 70 days; (2) The former main road, from Beiping via 18 stations (each station being a day's journey, so 18 days) to Xi'an, then another 18 stations to Lanzhou, then another 18 stations to Suzhou, then another 18 stations to Hami, and then another 18 stations to Dihua, taking a total of 90 days. Beiping to Xi'an is already half train and half automobile, taking about 4 days. Xi'an to Lanzhou is already accessible by automobile, taking about 4 or 5 days. Hami to Dihua is also accessible by automobile, taking about 4 or 5 days. If the automobile road from Lanzhou to Suzhou and from Suzhou to Hami is repaired, then Lanzhou to Suzhou will take about 4 or 5 days, and Suzhou to Hami will take about 4 or 5 days. Combining the automobile journeys, the original 90-day journey can be shortened to 21 or 22 days; (3) The formerly known Yangguan Avenue, which goes south to Xinjiang, Hotan, Yutian, and then to Has. This is only a rough description of the route. As for the detailed plan for developing transportation and opening up the Northwest, I will submit my humble opinions and discuss them in detail separately.

(9) Report from the Central Bureau of the Soviet Area to the Central Committee (April 19)

To the Central Committee: Regarding our recent combat situation, we can report on the following aspects:

Comrades Xiang Ying (transliteration), Bolinsky, Komornar, and three shortwave telegraph operators have all arrived here one after another. Xiang Ying arrived on January 11, and the Central Bureau was formally organized on the 15th. The Central Revolutionary Military Commission has also been established for many days. In addition to the members originally appointed by the Central Committee, the Central Bureau of the Soviet Area has elected Zhu De, Zheng Bingjun, Chen Yi, Zhu Yili, Peng Dehuai, and Lin Biao as members of the bureau at a recent expanded meeting. We request that this point be ratified.

(32) Letter from the Secretariat of the Pacific Trade Union Confederation to the National Labor Congress.

To the comrades of the National Labor Congress: After receiving the work plan of the congress in various districts directly under the Soviet Union, we have carefully examined it. In general, it is free from errors, but there are several points that must be clarified:

1. The issue of agricultural workers, namely, how to organize them into ordinary trade unions, and what is their relationship with poor farmers, especially with poor farmers' groups? The elements of this issue are obvious and without doubt, namely, that agricultural workers must be organized immediately and made into general trade unions, just like workers engaged in other industries. Agricultural workers' associations can be our most useful tool. Once this association is formed, we can use it to win over the hearts of poor farmers and benefit from the equalization of land revolution. Therefore, there must be very close contact and the closest relationship between agricultural workers, coolies, and poor farmers. In this way, agricultural workers, with the help of other artisans, can fulfill their leadership responsibilities. However, it seems that the organizational relationship between agricultural workers and poor farmers' groups is still unclear. Section B of the fourth section of the plan proposed by your congress says (middle peasants must unite with poor farmers' groups, and agricultural workers' associations can immediately join various poor farmers' groups and fulfill their leadership responsibilities to form a united front). Here, we should be more clear. Agricultural workers in any village should be organized in the same way as workers in other professions, each forming its own union. For example, a district branch of agricultural workers should be organized in a village, while the poor farmers in that village should form their own poor farmers' group. Agricultural workers are the most aware of the hardships of the peasant class. With the help of more experienced civilians in the trade unions, they can take the initiative in everything and fulfill their leadership responsibilities in organizing matters in poor farmers' groups. However, these agricultural workers, even if they are organized into groups, or as a district branch of a village, do not join the poor farmers' groups as members. They often hold regular meetings with poor farmers at that time, and hold joint meetings, and at the meeting, these groups often send their own representatives, just like brothers in the same association. Also, agricultural workers and poor farmers oppose landlords, moneylenders, the Kuomintang, and other warlords, in order to seek the complete victory of the equalization of land revolution. Both have the same immediate interests, but the farming workers' group must be maintained and developed into a general trade union, uniting with the revolutionary trade unions in the current Soviet Union-administered areas and the National Labor Congress, and under their command and control. The poor farmers' groups are not independent organizations, they are established within a village, and their duties are to be carried out under the orders of the Soviet administrator of that village. The only duty that they should fulfill is to assist the Soviet administrator in implementing the equalization of land revolution, and to fight against the forces of the Kulaks (rich peasants). This is why all farming workers must participate in the work of the poor farmers' groups, and the agricultural workers' associations must fulfill their leadership responsibilities in this important activity. In addition, coolies and artisans may also participate. Therefore, we propose that the above-mentioned items should be inserted into the draft, so as to avoid any misunderstanding of the meaning of the reorganization of the agricultural workers' associations in the countryside and the annexation of the poor farmers' groups by the agricultural workers' associations. There is also (We must firmly oppose the immediate adoption of collective farming. This attempt at collectivization is entirely initiated by the peasants, is out of the peasants' free will, and is without any external pressure) in the same section of the draft. There are also cases where farmers voluntarily organize groups for the purpose of making full use of their property. If we encounter such a situation, we will not prohibit or prevent it. The same section of the draft also discusses two types of farmers and two forms of agricultural workers' associations: (1) agricultural workers' associations; (2) short-term workers' associations (the organization of short-term workers' associations is temporarily placed under the guidance of agricultural workers' associations). We propose that the draft sets up two different organizations, which is easy to cause disputes, so one item must be deleted. Only one agricultural workers' association should be set up in a village or county. Its short-term workers can join the short-term workers' section of the association. Anyone who takes on regular work, or short-term work, or occasional work, or only takes on work in a certain season of the year, can be regarded as an agricultural worker and join the short-term workers' section of the agricultural workers' association. Anyone who has obtained a piece of land after the peasant revolution, and is still a land worker at some time, can be classified into this category. Some people think that there are no more agricultural workers after the land distribution, so there is no need for agricultural workers' associations. We must make every effort to attack this fallacy.

2. The section on (systematic development and leadership of the workers' class struggle) in the draft is generally correct, but we have one more proposal, namely, that any instructions you draw up for comrades who are going to work in the Soviet areas must insert Article 8 of the draft labor law regarding the right to strike, or record all of it in it (Under Soviet law, trade unions have the freedom of action, the right of organization, the right to express declarations, negotiate, and conclude treaties). We must declare the organization and leadership of workers' struggles in order to implement the provisions of the labor law.

Page 12

Before the labor law is implemented, that is, to implement the principles detailed in our draft.) This is not only the right of our class trade unions in the Soviet areas, but also their due responsibility. The distinction between state-owned enterprises and private enterprises is very important for strikes, and it is recognized that state-owned enterprises in the current stage of class struggle are in urgent need of defending the Red Army and the Soviet government. However, this is not to say that we prohibit strikes in state-owned enterprises. The basic provisions of the Labor Law, such as the eight-hour work day and the minimum wage, must be strictly observed in state-owned enterprises. If the military situation in the Red Army and the Soviet areas requires the concentration of forces to supply armaments and food, workers can voluntarily increase their working hours under the leadership of the trade union to protect the safety of the Soviet government. However, this kind of action cannot take the form of a Soviet order, and the same is true for the prohibition of strikes. This is the most important propaganda work and organizational work of the trade union.

3. Regarding the organizational work in the Soviet area in Section 6, we also have a proposal, namely, that special attention must be paid to the necessity of trade unions having true proletarian leaders. This leadership staff,

Must be selected by the workers themselves from among the workers' class, in order to ensure the safety of the Soviet government and the Red Army. According to our opinion, a paragraph should be inserted in the section on the internal daily life and activities of the trade union, namely, the issue of regular meetings and membership review meetings, as well as the issue of voluntary membership fees. However, membership fees must be paid on time to ensure the financial security of the trade union.

4. Regarding the relationship between the trade union and the Soviet organs in Section 10, according to our opinion, a paragraph should be inserted, namely, that for the workers of our trade union in the urban and rural soviets, trade union members should actively participate in the local Soviet elections, so that the most proletarian-conscious factory workers, handicraftsmen, and agricultural workers in the Soviet areas can work hand in hand with poor farmers. The (Labor Committee) and (Labor Inspector) must be directly introduced and appointed by the trade union. In addition, the personnel of organizations such as social insurance and labor security cooperatives must also be directly appointed by the trade union. In the section on production control, how to control production in private enterprises should be explained. The labor management committee elected by the workers and directly guided by the trade union must first pay attention to ensuring that the provisions of the labor law are implemented, and that employers or their agents do not engage in any sabotage or counter-revolutionary actions, so that the workers of private enterprises are adequately prepared to support the Red Army and the Soviet Union. These committees should also be given the right to inspect the business accounts of private enterprises in order to implement the provisions of the Labor Law. The control and management of workers in state-owned enterprises are very different from the special functions of the workers' control committees in the above-mentioned private enterprises, and we should distinguish between them.

5. Regarding the unemployment issue in Section 9, one point that must be given special attention is that the Soviet government is currently fighting a life-and-death struggle with the enemy, and this struggle cannot be successful in the short term, so the work of dealing with mass unemployment should not be added to the Soviet government's body. Enlist the best members of the unemployed workers into the Red Army, and provide unemployment relief from the social insurance organs stipulated by the Labor Law (this is difficult to implement for a while), and prepare an unemployed workers' fund, which is managed by the trade union. All of these are the main plans at present.

6. It is important to form all transport workers, such as boatmen, coachmen, sedan chair carriers, and rickshaw pullers, into a united association in the draft, but we must distinguish between water transport, land transport, and railway transport. At present, these three should be organized into various industrial unions separately. Those engaged in water transport (including port workers) can form a union, railway workers can form a railway workers' union, and other land transport workers can form another union.

7. Special attention must be paid to the organization of women and young people. One important point that must be noted is that women or young people do not need to independently organize a union. Female workers and male workers can join the same union, and their obligations and rights are the same as male workers. Female workers over the age of fourteen must also be organized, and can also join the trade union, and have the same rights. The youth department can be set up in the trade union, and is directly managed and guided by the trade union.

8. The following items should be inserted in the section on propaganda work: disseminating the activity plan of the Secretariat of the Pacific Trade Union Confederation, breaking down local feelings and isolationism, the issue of international interdependence, the struggle of workers in other colonial and semi-colonial countries and imperialist countries, pointing out the need to report to the Secretariat of the Pacific Trade Union Confederation on time and contact it. Secretariat of the Pacific Trade Union Confederation (incomplete)

Establishment of the Liaoning All-Circles Flood Relief Association 82

The target donation amount is set at 500,000 yuan

However, Zhang Xueliang advocates providing relief with grain

Shenyang Correspondence: Liaoning circles believe that the Yangtze and Han river floods are severe and that it is not enough to provide relief without concentrating the strength of the whole country. Previously, the Party Department specially convened the (Liaoning Circles Relief Association for the Yangtze and Huai River Floods), which had convened two preparatory meetings. At 10:30 am on the 5th, the association convened an establishment meeting in the Party Department auditorium of the province. More than 40 representatives from all walks of life, including Chen Wenxue, Zhu Guangmu, and Ms. Su Bei, attended the meeting. More than 40 members of the Provincial Party Department, including Xing Shilian and Li Shaoyuan, attended the meeting. Xing Shilian chaired the meeting. After the meeting began, the organizational outline of the conference was first approved. The content was based on the draft method submitted by Chen Wenxue at the discussion meeting on the 4th. After consulting various opinions, the wording was slightly increased or decreased, but the principle was not changed. The name of the conference was then changed to (Liaoning All-Circles Relief Association for National Floods). The organization was changed to a committee system, and leaders of various agencies and legal entities were elected as members of the committee. Zhang Xueliang was elected as the chairman, Zang Shiyi was the vice chairman, and Chen Wenxue was the general secretary. They would follow the chairman's instructions to lead the directors and directors of each department to handle daily affairs. The candidates would be drafted by Chen and submitted to the board meeting on the 7th for approval, and then they could officially start working. The donation amount was temporarily set at 500,000 yuan, and 100,000 yuan would be borrowed from the banking sector in advance for remittance. The meeting period was set for three months. The establishment telegram and notice of the conference had been drafted by the Provincial Party Department. After being read aloud at the scene, they were handed over to Chen Wenxue to submit to the Vice Chairman Zang Shiyi for review, and it was decided to send them out on the 7th. The meeting adjourned at 12:30. The following items were resolved on the same day:

(1) This association is jointly organized by the provincial government, military, academic, agricultural, industrial, commercial, women, banking, transportation sectors, and other social groups. (2) This association is a committee system. Zhang Xueliang is elected as the chairman, Zang Shiyi is elected as the vice chairman, and there is one general secretary, and Chen Wenxue is publicly appointed to take the position. There are also three groups: General Affairs, Fundraising, and Publicity. Each group has a director, who is appointed by the general secretary. (3) Leaders from all circles are members of this association. (4) The minimum amount to be raised is 500,000 yuan. (5) Political organs in the provincial capital and various counties are guided by the provincial government, the military is assigned by the Border Defense Department, agriculture, industry and commerce are assigned by various guilds, the academic community is assigned by the Education Department, the banking sector is assigned by the banking groups, the press is assigned by the Press Association, individual families are assigned by women's groups, and entertainment events are assigned by the Public Security Bureau and the Boy Scouts. In addition, artists are solicited for various works to be auctioned off as donations. (6) The official silver firm is the collection agency of this association. (7) Individuals who donate more than 100 yuan have the right to designate a certain place for relief. (8) All donations are requested to be remitted free of charge by various banks, and various railways and ferries are requested to transport relief supplies free of charge. (9) This association convenes a board meeting once every two weeks.

Another message, the Liaoning Flood Relief Association has been established, and the donation amount is set at 500,000 yuan. 100,000 yuan will be borrowed from the banking sector first to remit to the Central Government, and the rest will be remitted one after another. Grain is also accepted. This is the method decided by the Flood Relief Association. Deputy Zhang sent a telegram to Shenyang, ordering the five northeastern provinces to assist with 30,000 dan of grain (a large dou in Fengtian, which is equivalent to about 60,000 shi in the south, worth 320,000 yuan at current market prices), without mentioning raising cash. The Political Committee meeting yesterday decided that the Northeast has been in financial difficulties recently and has a surplus of grain, so the relief will be provided by transporting grain instead of cash. The 30,000 dan will be distributed among the five provinces, with 8,000 for Liaoning, 7,000 for Jilin, 5,500 each for Heilongjiang and Harbin, and 4,000 for Rehe, half sorghum and half millet. They will be collected in Liaoning and Yingkou in the future, and transported by southern ships. All provinces have been notified. This method conflicts with the Liaoning Flood Relief Association, and the association may change its method, but it is not yet known. (September 5)

Wuhu Express Letter 83

▲ In order to prepare for setting up commissioners in various provinces in the future to handle post-flood relief, the National Government's Flood Relief Committee has specially appointed Zhang Ru, Zhao Shouyu, Li Jinzhang, and Yuan Shan as flood inspection commissioners for the four provinces of Anhui, Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi. Zhang arrived in Wuhu yesterday and immediately contacted the county government. Today, he personally went to the disaster area for inspection, and then went to Fanchang and other counties in southern Anhui, and then went to central and northern Anhui for inspection.

▲ Sanshan Town, Fanchang County, which is 40 li away from Wuhu, was recently raided by about 300 bandits from Wuwei. They were riding in more than 20 civilian boats, parked in the middle of the Jiayi River, with complete firearms and flags painted with knives and axes. They landed and caused trouble, and planned to occupy Jitou Mountain as a defensive measure. After Fanchang County urgently transferred a large number of police teams, together with the self-defense regiments of nearby townships, they surrounded and attacked from both sides the night before. The bandits also resisted stubbornly. After several hours of fierce fighting, more than 140 bandits were killed on the spot, more than 40 were captured alive, 40 long guns were seized, and more than 20 hostages were rescued. The remaining bandits have now fled.

▲ Regarding the Wuhu rapeseed export issue, rice merchants said that rapeseed exports are not exclusively sold to Japan, and there are also sales markets in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. They have requested that the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Association postpone the ban on exports. However, the Anti-Japanese Association held a meeting today and resolved that the rapeseed transported out by Taikoo and Jardine Matheson in recent days is mostly resold to the Japanese. From today onwards, they will still be detained across the board, and the lighter workers will be ordered to stop handling them.

▲ Qian Danwu, a special investigator from the Central Relief Committee, and Wen Yi from the Provincial Committee, went from Wuhu to Fanchang to investigate. The entire county has no land without water, and no homes are not disaster-stricken. There are no villages, and more than 2,000 people have drowned, and more have committed suicide. They have sent a special telegram to the Central Government, requesting immediate assistance.

▲ The Anhui Education Department believes that the flood in Anhui Province this time is severe, and the impact on schools in various places is significant. A complete investigation and reorganization is necessary. In addition to dispatching school inspectors Li Guanglie and Deng Jixuan to inspect various counties, they have also dispatched Section Chief Yang Zhongming to inspect Wuhu and nearby counties. The number of new and old students attending school, as well as the damage to school supplies, and the methods and opinions for reorganization in the future must be thoroughly investigated and verified.

▲ At 2:00 pm today, the Wuhu County Government convened a flood relief meeting for all circles, attended by more than 50 representatives from various agencies and organizations. They discussed the method of universally distributing emergency relief throughout the disaster area and resolved to purchase 6,000 bags of flour and reed mats, etc., and distribute them in six major districts on the 13th. In addition to the heads of the township public security bureaus and the heads of the autonomous public offices, 30 people automatically signed up to participate on the spot by the county head of the Public Security Bureau. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 pm. (September 8)

Local Correspondence

Qingpu 84

A Water Police Informant Killed by Bandits: Bao Liansheng, a water police informant in this county, had considerable success in investigating bandit traces. This time, Mr. Bao personally went to a bandit den to investigate, was captured alive by the bandits, and was tragically drowned in the Lian River. His mother, upon hearing the news, was exceedingly grieved and instructed people to retrieve the body. The team headquarters, upon receiving the report, went to the scene of the incident for an on-site investigation.

Establishment of Sewing Workshop in Prison: The prison in this county, in order to provide inmates with a skill for making a living upon their release in the future, has successively established various workshops. Recently, a sewing workshop was added, staffed by skilled technicians from Jiangsu and Guangdong.

Songjiang 85

Bandit Leader Lu Yaosheng and Others Executed by Firing Squad: Lu Yaosheng, a pseudo-regiment commander under the command of Ah Shu, a bandit leader of Lake Tai, was captured by the Fengxian County police team and transferred to the Songhu Pacification Sub-district Command for interrogation. He confessed without denial to forming a gang to kidnap and rob various cities and towns in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Additionally, bandits Zhang Aliu, Wu Ayun (also known as Wang Liansheng), Yang Agen, Lu Aming (also known as Lu Zugen), and Sun Tuozi and five others, bandits active in the Quan Gong Ting New Town area, were all clearly interrogated and sentenced to death. The sentences were submitted to Zhang, the Jiangsu Pacification Commissioner, and approved by telegram for execution. After receiving the telegram, Commander Cao signed and brought the bandit leader Lu Yaosheng and others to the headquarters, verified their identities, and had them bound. After taking photographs, police escorted them on a parade through the busy city for a week before executing them by firing squad at the Yu Huang Ge execution grounds. When the bandit leader Lu Yaosheng and others were brought out of the prison gate, seeing the crowded onlookers, they knew their death was near. They chatted and laughed freely, looking around at the crowd, and their expressions did not change until the execution. They can truly be said to be the most extreme examples of those who disregard the law and are not afraid of death.

Bandit Leader Lu Yaosheng Photographed Before Execution 86

(Photographed by Da Zhonghua Photo Studio, Songjiang)

Local Gentry Telegraphs for Urgent Repair of Embankment: The first section of the Jinshanwei seawall in this county was severely impacted by heavy rain and strong waves for six consecutive days. The embankment patrolman deeply feared that it would be breached, and with the autumn flood season approaching rapidly, the consequences of not taking preventive measures would be enormous. Yesterday, local gentry Geng Daochong, Cai Guanghui, and others urgently telegraphed Governor Ye of the province, stating: "Various sections of the Songjiang seawall west of the pond are historically known to be vulnerable. This summer, wind, rain, and storm tides have eroded and threatened to breach the embankment. The Chamber of Commerce has already telegraphed the province to appeal for assistance. Unexpectedly, on September 6th, the second section is also on the verge of failure, making the situation even more critical. If preventive measures are not taken promptly, the autumn flood season will bring even greater disaster. We earnestly request that you dispatch personnel to urgently repair the embankment as quickly as possible to protect the lives of all the people."

Suzhou 87

Telegraphic Request to Stop Opening the East Dam: The Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce, based on reports that the authorities were planning to open the East Dam, telegraphed Governor Ye of Jiangsu Province yesterday (the 9th), stating, "Reports indicate that Gaochun is flooded and that there are plans to open the East Dam. If this is implemented, all counties south of the Yangtze River will definitely be submerged. Considering the tragic robberies in Gao and Shao, we are sending this telegram to request a swift halt to the opening and to prevent further urgent pleas.” The county government also expressed its views on this matter.

Raping of a Thirteen-Year-Old Girl: Zhou Laoer, a wine shop owner residing at No. 33 Xihuaqiao Lane, aged thirty-seven, lured Ah Genjin, a thirteen-year-old girl residing at Tangju's house in Qianwanli Bridge, to Room No. 7 of the Tailu Hotel last month and raped her twice. Tang Ajin suffered severe injuries to her lower body but dared not speak about it at her mother’s place. Unexpectedly, the injuries worsened daily, and her lower body even ulcerated. Only then did she tell her mother, who reported it to the First Public Security Bureau. Zhou has not been apprehended. Zhou's cohabiting couple, Gao Shuangxi and his wife, were detained by the bureau for questioning about Zhou's whereabouts. On the night of the 8th, Zhou Laoer was finally arrested and taken to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Changshu 88

Notorious Bandit Zheng Ming Executed: Zheng Ming, a maritime bandit from Dongxing Township in this county, committed a crime in Shanghai. After his arrest, Detective Captain Zhu Shunqing brought Zheng back. At the same time, Zheng’s associates, Hu Peilin and others, were also brought to Changshu. According to Zheng's repeated confessions, he made no denials, stating precisely which crimes he committed and which he did not, consistent to the end. Knowing that he would certainly be sentenced to death, he asked the judge to execute him as soon as possible. After receiving the confession, the county government telegraphed the province for instructions. On the evening of the 8th, the county government received a telegram from the province authorizing the execution of Zheng by firing squad. At seven o'clock the next morning, police and public security officers went to the East Gate Prison to bring Zheng out. At that time, many members of the public went to watch. When Zheng was brought out of the prison gate and saw this scene, he asked the bailiff, "Is this my day to go to heaven?" The bailiff did not answer. Zheng laughed wildly until he reached the county government, where he was questioned by Judge Shen Cheng about any final words. He replied that he had none, and along the way, he loudly sang excerpts from the opera "Mao Yanshou". Soon, he was taken to the execution ground and immediately shot. Zheng Ming was from Yancheng, Jiangbei, grew up in Wangshi Town, Changshu, and was twenty-four years old.

Wuxi 89

Sentenced to Imprisonment for Carnal Knowledge of a Young Girl: Ye Ziping, the owner of a lead sheet shop at Kuatangqiao outside the South Gate, aged sixty-one, had carnal knowledge of Xie Axi, a fifteen-year-old female worker at the Taifu Silk Factory near Taqiao. The Public Security Bureau detained him and sent him to the county court, where he was interrogated and detained for several months. Yesterday afternoon at five o'clock, Judge Liang opened the court and sentenced Ye to four years of imprisonment for the crime of carnal knowledge of a girl under the age of sixteen. Ye expressed his dissatisfaction with the verdict. However, his wife, Wu, upon hearing the verdict, cried loudly and, because her husband declared his dissatisfaction, rushed to Judge Liang's table, stating that she was desperately poor and unable to appeal, and pleading for a reduction of her husband's sentence. Judge Liang ordered the court police to persuade her to leave. Wu had no choice but to leave in tears.

Business Tax Bureau Conducts Re-inspections: There are currently only eighteen business tax bureaus in Jiangsu Province. In counties with finance bureaus, the finance bureau chief also serves as the business tax bureau chief. In counties without finance bureaus, the county magistrate also serves, paid for by the province. In this county, the annual business tax for various industries in the urban area is approximately 70,000 yuan. The annual tax for various industries in the rural area is approximately 10,000 yuan, totaling approximately 80,000 yuan per year. Currently, the first batch of taxes paid by more than eighty industries in the urban area's Chamber of Commerce has been delivered to the bureau. Various industries not in the Chamber of Commerce are directly collected by the bureau. Only a few towns in the rural area have paid. The bureau is actively working on this. The bureau is currently issuing business licenses to various industries in the urban area that have paid their taxes. Once this is completed, personnel will be dispatched to conduct re-inspections.

Jiangyin 90

Petition for Dispatch of Personnel to Settle Arrears in Education Funds: Jiangyin's education funds have been in arrears for four and a half months. Teachers are teaching on empty stomachs, making it difficult to continue. Salary-seeking riots are likely to occur everywhere. The treatment of teachers in Jiangyin is originally very meager. The monthly salary of junior teachers is only seven or eight yuan. Even if they are paid in full every month, it is still difficult to make a living, let alone with such a large amount in arrears. How can they teach with peace of mind? Lu Lifan, the director of the education bureau, attributed the arrears to the ineffective collection of land taxes by the finance bureau. He previously submitted separate reports to the provincial government's finance and education departments, strictly ordering the finance bureau to expedite collection. Director Shen of the finance bureau replied, stating that there were no arrears and that there was no misappropriation. The education department then ordered the education bureau to verify in detail and report the amounts of assessed and collected taxes, as well as the amount of education funds received by the bureau, for future reference. After receiving the order, Director Lu checked the bureau's budget book. The total amount of assessed taxes for the 17th, 18th, and 19th years was 515,367 yuan. The finance bureau's book showed that 317,708 yuan, 7 jiao, 5 fen, and 2 li of education funds had been collected, including the first half of the 16th year. After checking this against the amount received by the bureau, there was no significant discrepancy. The bureau's arrears amounted to 246,136 yuan. The finance bureau's book showed that 221,620 yuan, 6 jiao, and 4 fen, 6 li of education funds had not been collected, a difference of 24,515 yuan, 3 jiao, 5 fen, and 4 li. This was due to the poor harvest in the 18th year. Whether the numbers match or not requires the finance bureau to provide the number of tenants and the amount of land, so that it can be calculated. As the finance bureau's book shows that 221,620 yuan, 6 jiao, and 4 fen, 6 li have not been collected, accounting for more than 43% of the assessed amount, the location of the arrears, whether it is misappropriated by the finance bureau, or due to official arrears or civil arrears, cannot be understood without a thorough investigation. Therefore, the education department is asked to strictly order the finance bureau to expedite the collection of the outstanding education funds to alleviate the urgent need and, on the one hand, send personnel to clean up the situation together in order to maintain education.

Nantong 91

Military Engineers Repair Collapsed Culverts Along the River: The culverts along the river in Nantong were mostly collapsed due to previous storm tides. The local collapse protection association is consulting with the stationed 280th Regiment in Tong to implement military engineering repairs. Work began on the 8th.

Disaster Relief Boats Continue to Operate in Taixian County: The flood disaster in Taixian County is severe. The Nantong County Government, following a provincial telegram, continues to hire small steamers to go to Taixian to rescue disaster victims from danger. On the 8th, personnel sent by the disaster relief association towed twenty Dahulun steamers and civilian boats for use. The Tongyi Relief Team in Dongtai telegraphed the county government on the 8th, stating that 300 disaster victims from Xinghua and 400 disaster victims from Dongtai have been sent to Tong on special ships.

Provincial Military Law Department Transfers Counter-Revolutionary Prisoners: The Provisional Military Law Review Department of the Provincial Government transferred Chen Hetian and other counter-revolutionary prisoners from Lianshui, Taixing, and other counties who had already been sentenced to prison terms. The Zhenjiang County Government sent a police team to escort them to Tong and imprison them in the fourth prison.

Zhenjiang 92

Request to Restore Shipping on the Canal: The Temporary Charity Relief Association for Water Disaster in Jiangbei requested that the Chamber of Commerce and Temporary Relief Association for Water Disaster in Huai'an and Gaoyou counties send a telegram to request the immediate resumption of shipping to facilitate travel and to alleviate commercial difficulties due to the receding canal water. They also received a letter from Leng and Lu, the two directors of the association, stating that the Zhenqing and Zhentai steamers should urgently resume traffic to facilitate relief efforts and convenience commerce. This was immediately submitted to the association's fifth standing committee meeting, which resolved to request the shipping association to investigate and comply. Yesterday, a letter was also sent to the provincial government ordering the shipping association to comply in order to facilitate relief efforts and convenience transportation. It is expected that the resumption of the two small steamers will not be far off. However, it is heard that the shipping association is concerned because the previous Zhu Fang steamer was burned by rioters at the Yangtze Bridge. Although the government recognized the compensation, it has not yet been resolved. If it is desired to resume service this time, the government must provide adequate protection and resolve the donation losses as soon as possible.

Yangzhou 93

Commissioner’s Office Executes Kidnapper: On the morning of the 8th, the Commissioner’s Office executed the bandit Sun Jichen at the Kangshan execution grounds. The prisoner was the main culprit in the Zhang Shaofeng kidnapping and ransom case. He was previously apprehended and handed over to the office by the Jiangdu County Public Security Bureau. He confessed that he had contacted the ransom note and extorted 6,900 yuan from Zhang Guo's family, which he handed over to the bandit gang, which he did not deny. He was sentenced to death in accordance with Article 2 of the Regulations for the Punishment of Kidnappers.

Hangzhou 94

The Main Culprit in the Xu Zhuoran Assassination Case Escorted to Hangzhou: In the case of the assassination of Xu Zhuoran in Fujian, the Hangzhou County District Court sentenced Ye Caizhen, Chen Yanxiang, and Chen Delin to not guilty. Lin Luo was sentenced to four years for privately possessing military weapons. The prosecutor investigating the case, Chen Huaming, and the plaintiff, Xu Ye’s family, did not accept the verdict and filed a public prosecution with the High Court. The three suspects in the case, Chen Chang, Zhang Jichang, and Liu Zhi, were escorted from Fujian. On August 11th, the First Criminal Court of the High Court summoned thirteen people, including the original plaintiffs, defendants, and criminals in the case, to open the trial. Because Chen Chang and Zhang Jichang were highly suspected, and the three defendants Ye Caizhen and others requested bail, it was ruled that they would each pay a bail of 20,000 yuan. Chen Jiageng, an overseas Chinese, bailed out Ye Caizhen and Chen Yanxiang with 40,000 yuan. It is now known that Lin Min, the main culprit who assassinated Xu, was captured by the Tong'an garrison in Fujian on June 19th. The High Court specially dispatched Shen Weiqing, a clerk of the Criminal Court, and four bailiffs to Fujian to escort him back. He was escorted to Hangzhou on the evening of the 8th. After being briefly questioned by the prosecutor, he was sent to the detention center to await trial.

Verdict Announced in the Case of Trafficking a Huge Amount of Red Pills: In the case of the seizure of a large batch of 400,000 red pills at the Jiang Qiannanxing Station, the main criminals Huang Chunyan, Yao Hairong, and Li Chucai, and six others, including Hong Peiyun, the owner of the Guotang business, Hong Youlan, the bookkeeper, and Shen Qing, the assistant manager of the Shenda Company, were arrested. After the investigation was completed, the verdict was announced yesterday. Huang Chunyan, Yao Hairong, and Li Chucai were each sentenced to three years of imprisonment and fined 2,000 yuan each for the crime of jointly trafficking in opium substitutes. Hong Peiyun, Hong Youlan, and Shen Qingde were each sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined 1,000 yuan each for the crime of joint transportation.

Shangyu 95

Dispute Over the Demarcation of Police Districts by the Public Security Bureau: The County Public Security Bureau previously divided the entire county into four police districts based on the revised Organizational Regulations of the Public Security Bureau of Zhejiang Province. The Fourth Branch Bureau divided Songxia into the first section and Lihai Office into the second section, and withdrew the police officers from the Lihai Office Public Security Sub-station belonging to Shaoxing. A police station was established in the territory of the Lihai Office, which belongs to Yu County. This caused opposition from all sectors of Lihai Office. The reason is that the Lihai Public Security Sub-station was established with the approval of local gentry Yang Zhaochun during the era when Qu Yingguang was the Zhejiang Patrol Envoy during the Republic of China and has been in existence for eighteen years. The province approved the establishment of the police bureau because the area is indeed a strategic coastal location. Considering the actual situation of the area, it is twenty li away from Songxia, and it is extremely inconvenient to merge with Songxia and establish a police station. It is proposed to follow the precedent of the recent dispute between the Linpu Public Security Sub-stations of Shaoxing and Su counties over the jurisdiction of the police district, and unanimously advocate retaining the original Lihai Office Public Security Sub-station. On the 31st of last month, a representative was dispatched to order the Lihai Office Public Security Sub-station to postpone the abolishment, and the original proposal to implement it from the 1st of September was suspended. It is now known that various sectors of the town have been meeting for days to carefully plan a method of retention.
