Shanghai County Restores the Bounding System 142

Undertaking the Collection of Xin Cao Grain Tax

To Be Implemented Before October 15

In Shanghai County, households that have not completed the payment of the busy season grain tax outside the quota have been responsible for urging payment by the bounding industry in the past. The annual payment has long been effective. Since the change to township chiefs last year, the collection of taxes has been sluggish. It is difficult for township chiefs to take care of the local autonomy and difficult to compare with the bounding industry, which specializes in the matter. The county government has recently reported from the first district office requesting the restoration of the bundling industry system. When the Finance Bureau was ordered to formulate implementation measures, the bureau director Wang found that neighboring Songjiang, Qingpu, Nanhui and other counties had not eliminated the previous system. The upper town is the same, and the bundling industry system can be restored. When the measures were drafted, the county government ordered the approval, and the bureau and the district chiefs carefully handled it. Director Wang convened district chiefs to the bureau the day before to discuss and resolved to restore the bundling industry from the 20th year of the Republic. On the one hand, the districts informed the township heads to convene the original bounding industries and ordered them to resume the undertaking of the busy season affairs, and all of them were implemented before October 15. In addition to recording and reporting the resolutions to the county government, the bureau also informed the people of the county to know.

Rectifying the Autumn Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax 143

Notice from the Collection Branch

The Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Branch of Shanghai County sent a notice to various pharmacies and hotels yesterday, saying: "For notification, the Jiangsu Shangbao Chuanchongqi Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Bureau ordered that the tobacco and alcohol license tax has always been the nature of a contractor. The change to the commissioned office this time is to eliminate accumulated malpractices and rectify tax revenue. It is now found that pharmacies that operate medicinal alcohol and restaurants and hotels that also operate tobacco and alcohol should pay taxes separately in accordance with the regulations. In addition to the separate orders, the director should immediately follow the instructions, immediately investigate and verify the above-mentioned merchants, break away from personal feelings, and earnestly rectify them. Starting from this autumn, order them to pay taxes and obtain licenses in order to comply with the regulations and maintain the national tax, and do not slightly conceal any faults. The group collection staff of our office have been ordered to collect and order the payment of taxes and obtain licenses. According to Article 4 of the detailed rules promulgated by the ministry, if the merchants who have obtained licenses have not applied for a new license after the deadline in the previous article, the competent tax collection agency shall warn them in writing. If they still do not apply for a new license within ten days from the date of delivery of the warning letter, in addition to ordering them to pay taxes and exchange licenses, they shall be fined from one-tenth to two-tenths of the tax payable per quarter. If they still delay in applying for a new license one month after the date of delivery of the warning letter, they shall be deemed to be operating without a license and shall be handled in accordance with Article 8 of the Provisional Regulations on Tobacco and Alcohol Business Licenses: (1) For the first offense, a fine of one to two times the tax payable per quarter shall be imposed; (2) For the second offense, a fine of three to ten times the tax payable per quarter shall be imposed; (3) For the third offense, they shall not be allowed to operate. The store has been urged to pay taxes and obtain a license before the deadline, which has been exceeded. It is hereby notified that the store should follow the instructions and pay taxes and obtain a license at the office on the day, and do not play around or violate them, so as not to interfere with the penalty. This is the most important thing."

Mr. Wu Tingsheng, Chairman of the Shanghai Cigarette Factory Association, has spared no effort in organizing the association's affairs since taking office. Housheng Yarn Factory Workers Sue Representatives for Embezzling Huge Sum of Dismissal Compensation of 210,000 Yuan, Accusing Representatives of Embezzling All. The Housheng Ziji Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Lan Road has been established for many years, with thousands of male and female workers. Unexpectedly, on December 21st of last year, the yarn factory suddenly announced its closure. When the news came, all the workers were shocked and distressed, and because it was the end of the year, it was difficult to find work, and they did not know how to make a living. Therefore, nine foremen, Cai Huansheng, Yan Baobao, Yang Fobao, Yu Asi, Jiang Erlang, Jiang Yaozhen, Wang Guansong, Chen Songyun, Yuan Xie Kang, etc., volunteered to be representatives to negotiate with the management, requesting five months' wages and three months' retirement pay. Later, because the investor, Bei Runsheng, and the manager, Li Dixian, did not agree, Cai Huansheng and others hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to file a complaint with the former French Concession Public Concession. As a result, a settlement was reached, and the case was withdrawn. However, the workers learned that the investor had paid 210,000 yuan as dismissal compensation for the workers, which was given to the workers' representatives. However, the workers have not received a single penny to this day, and it is obvious that the representatives have embezzled it. Therefore, three workers, Shen Dalang, Huang Jinbao, and Zhu Haibao, hired lawyers Wang Zuxun and Xue Jiaqi to file a complaint against the nine representatives, Cai Huansheng, et al., with the First Special District Local Court, accusing them of breach of trust and embezzlement, and requesting that witnesses Li Dixing, Yuan Runsheng, Jiang Yiping, and Xue Gansheng be summoned to court for questioning. At 2:30 p.m. yesterday, Judge Wu Tingqi presided over a hearing in the Second Criminal Court. None of the defendants appeared in court, only the plaintiffs Shen and Huang, accompanied by their attorneys, were present. The plaintiffs' attorney began by stating the circumstances of the case. Then, Judge Wu asked the two plaintiffs what they were accusing the defendants of. According to Huang Jinbao, they were accusing Cai Huansheng and others of embezzling the dismissal compensation. He asked, "How much in total?" He replied, "210,000 yuan." He asked, "How much should each person receive?" He replied, "210,000 yuan." He asked, "Each person..." The case had already been filed with the former French Concession Public Concession, and it was strange to abandon the original trial court and pursue the matter in this court. Moreover, this case is of a civil nature and does not involve criminal matters. A lawsuit should first be filed with the Civil Court. Therefore, he ordered that whether a crime was committed in this case should first be resolved through a civil lawsuit, and then this case would be processed. The Apprentice at the Pharmacy Killed the Shop Owner in the Middle of the Night Because the Loan Was Not Granted and He Was Drunk. Ma Youzhi's Injuries Were Still Minor. The Murderer Claimed It Was Due to Jealousy. Xu Guozhang from Changzhou was an apprentice at the Jiuhetang Pharmacy at No. 1039 Dongyouheng Road, owned by Ma Youzhi from Zhenjiang. He had previously borrowed 50 yuan from Ma, but Ma only agreed to give him five silver dollars. Xu was dissatisfied, thinking that the owner had earned hundreds of yuan recently, so why be stingy with such a small amount? He harbored evil intentions and thought of harming him. The night before, he secretly went out and bought a large bottle of sorghum wine and brought it back, drinking to intoxication with his colleague surnamed Xu. They each returned to their bedrooms. Unexpectedly, Xu became extremely drunk and rushed into Ma Youzhi's bedroom with a kitchen knife. It was already close to midnight, and Ma was sleeping soundly in bed, having a good dream. Xu raised the kitchen knife and slashed at Ma's head, chest, and waist. Ma woke up in extreme pain and screamed for help. The apprentices heard the alarm and opened the shop door, flying to report to the nearby Chinese constable at No. 1168. They captured Xu, seized the kitchen knife, and took him to the Huishan Police Station, reporting to the head constable, who ordered him to be detained. The injured person was taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Fortunately, the injuries were minor and he was expected to recover. Yesterday morning, the police station escorted Xu Guozhang to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. According to the police station's attorney Zhang Tianyin, the defendant intended to plot to murder and seize property. The victim, Ma Youzhi, arrived in court with his injuries to testify about the situation at the time, claiming that he had 500-600 yuan in silver, which the defendant had seen, which led to this incident, etc. When questioned, the defendant confessed that he was in a good mood last night and drank half a catty of sorghum wine with his colleague Mr. Xu, which led to the trouble due to drunkenness. The purpose was actually a female tenant, because the owner and I both wanted to have relations with her, and I had previously been scolded by him, harboring resentment in my heart, so I committed this act in a drunken stupor, please have mercy. Judge Xiao Xie Fen verified the confession and ordered the defendant to be detained for further interrogation after witnesses were summoned. The Bronze Sand Lightship Will Be Temporarily Removed: The First Thousand and Tenth Notice of the Patrol Works Division of the Customs and Maritime Affairs Department of the Customs Department states that the bronze sand lightship, which belongs to the Jianghai Customs Tax Department and is anchored at the Yangtze River waterway entrance within the boundary, will be temporarily removed around October 6th of this year and will be replaced by another lightship. The implementation will take place at that time, and no further notice will be given. The replacement ship will be decorated in red and will not have a name on the side. It will be equipped with a fourth-order lens white light, which will flash once every ten seconds, that is, five seconds of light and five seconds of darkness. In clear weather, it can be seen for eleven nautical miles. In case of heavy fog or gloomy weather, a fog bell will be sounded once every fifteen seconds. In order to indicate the direction of the bow, a white light will be hung at the bow from sunset to sunrise, with the light 12 feet above the deck. Once the bronze sand lightship is repaired, it will still be anchored in its original location, and the replacement lightship will be removed. The implementation will take place at that time, and no further notice will be given. Therefore, all ships are hereby notified to pay close attention and remember the details in order to avoid errors and omissions. Be sure not to forget. This notice is hereby given on September 4th of the 20th year of the Republic of China. Xi Liman, Patrol Works Division. Reader's Letter: A Miss Writes: I am a young woman, and my level of education is in the second year of junior high school. I used to study at a church school and have now transferred to a midwifery school. Because I was adopted by my parents when I was young, and my parents have now given birth to a younger sister, my parents did not allow me to enter the midwifery school before I entered it. However, I resolutely wanted to enter, and it has been a year now. Unfortunately, my father's business has stopped, and our financial situation is becoming increasingly difficult. It takes two years to graduate from midwifery school, plus a half-year internship. The cost is very high, so my parents do not allow me to continue in this school. However, although I am a woman, I also have the ambition to be self-reliant. If I drop out of school, wouldn't that be a pity? I remember the saying, "If you don't work hard when you are young, you will only regret it when you are old," and I can't help but sigh. I also think of the meaning of not giving up after a hundred setbacks, and I still want to enter this school. However, how can I bear the scolding and reproaches I receive every day? I hope that you, sir, can find me a suitable job or allow me to continue studying at the midwifery school. I humbly ask you to show me a good way and answer me in the newspaper. (Reply) We are very sympathetic to your situation, admire your ambition, and are very willing to help you solve your problems. However, this newspaper does not have a job placement agency, and we do not know what places need people, so we cannot help you find a job. You should ask others for an introduction. However, it is very difficult to find a job without a specialty. It is best to finish your studies at the midwifery school. Since your father is unable to continue providing you with tuition, can you find a way to borrow money from relatives and friends? Fortunately, you only have one year left to study. Or, borrow money to study for half a year first, and with your utmost efforts, get good grades. In the remaining half year, based on your qualifications as an excellent student, declare to the school that you are willing to be a hard-working student who provides services, and request free or reduced fees. Once you graduate, you can perform midwifery duties and use your income to repay your debts and show filial piety to your parents. Not only will you overcome the difficulties, but your family will be harmonious and your future will be infinitely bright. Everything in the world depends on human effort. Do not be discouraged. You must rely on your sincerity, muster your courage, and work hard in every possible way. Stamp for Communication. Letter to the Editor: Respected Sir, In your newspaper's "Local News" column on September 9th, there was a report about "Swindling 100,000 Yuan in Public Bonds," which involved our company. After investigation, it was found that the Wen Zhou Fu Zi Zhuang store clerks were involved in fraud, which has nothing to do with our company. After purchasing the bonds, the store temporarily deposited them with our company. On the morning of August 31st, our company received a registered letter from the store stating that they had sent a clerk, Zhu Ming, to Shanghai to claim the bonds based on the letter. Shortly after, Zhu Ming came to claim the bonds with the store's letter of credit. Our company checked the seals on both letters and found that they matched the historical seals, so they were returned. It was not until midnight that day that our company received a telegram from the store stating that the seal had been stolen by the store clerks. Therefore, this matter was caused by internal fraud within the store and was not due to our company being deceived. Subsequently, the manager of the store came to Shanghai to report the case to the police for investigation. All the investigation and detention matters were handled by the store itself and had nothing to do with our company. Please correct this to clarify the facts and avoid misunderstandings. Sincerely, Shanghai Tongyi Trust Company, September 9th.

Free Talk No Removing Garden Grass Zhaifu Talks About What I See People who go to Japan always want to know some stories about the Emperor. I also have this curiosity. One of my questions is what is the attitude of modern Japanese towards the Emperor? How is it different from before? While in Tokyo, I saw a book in the Ohashi Library called "The Emperor and the Proletariat," which I found very strange. After reading the contents of the book carefully, I learned that the author's purpose was to combine the Emperor with the working masses to overthrow the bourgeoisie in the middle. This is a whimsical strategy. According to Miyazaki Ryusuke, there are many people in this faction. The proletarian party said that the workers would never be fooled by this theory. In short, this faction is trying to win over the workers from the Emperor's position. I found a marginal note written in blue ink in this book: (With an annual income of 20 million, watching 1.5 million unemployed people freeze and starve with nowhere to turn, still having chrysanthemum banquets today and cherry blossom viewing tomorrow, how can such people be connected with the working masses!) It is not known whose handwriting this marginal note is. Presumably it was written by a student. On January 16th of this year, I went to Momoyama to visit the Meiji Mausoleum. While I was on the mountain, there were also fifteen Japanese people who came to visit the mausoleum one after another, including farmers, old women from the countryside, children, retired soldiers from the countryside, and a worker. I stood there and carefully observed their behavior. Everyone respectfully knelt in front of the mausoleum to pray when they arrived. The children followed their parents and did the same. Only the worker stood there without bowing, looked for a moment, and then went down the mountain alone. Four Doctors Struggling in Russia Madam Yehua Who are the Four Doctors? They are Doctor of Medicine Fei Kunnian, Doctor of Law Yang Qi, Doctor of Letters Sun Pengxian, and Doctor of Engineering Xu Haiyu. The gentlemen set off from Germany and France this spring, returning to China via Siberia. They suffered hardships along the way in Soviet Russia. They extracted what Mr. Fei said to inform the countrymen to know about the experiences in Russia. ▲Traveling with the Elder Brother is Not Possible The third night of the train journey, they arrived in Moscow and rested for three and a half hours. They went to Chita. Tickets were checked along the way. The final destination on the Four Doctors' passports was Vladivostok, but the train tickets were for Manzhouli. The ticket inspector believed that the passports and train tickets did not match and was furious. He stopped their return journey. The four of them had not thought about this beforehand, and they were all saddened by this. They asked about the solution. Some said to telegraph to Moscow, and some said to turn back. They were at a loss for what to do. They met an old Polish man who planned to go to Harbin for business. He interceded with the ticket inspector, and they got off the train in Chita at midnight. They consulted with the stationmaster, but he was not there. They wandered in a foreign land in the icy and snowy ground. ▲The Doctor Suddenly Disappears That night, they met a detective. The detective was kind and volunteered to handle the passport negotiations. At 9 a.m., the detective left his post and arranged to go to the passport office together in the afternoon. While they were discussing, Dr. Xu suddenly disappeared. They searched everywhere but could not find him. Everyone suspected that something unexpected had happened. After half an hour, Xu happily arrived, saying that he had met a fellow villager from Shanxi who could help with the passport. The three were overjoyed and went to see him together. Unexpectedly, the fellow villager was a bill collector at a hotel. His residence was as dirty as a stove. The place was small and crowded. They looked at each other in dismay. However, there was nowhere else to stay, so they had to endure it. The food was worse than that of rickshaw pullers in Shanghai. Pickled vegetable and shredded pork soup were considered delicacies. The tableware was dirty and broken, and there was no way to use it. However, they were hungry and thirsty, so they had to force themselves to eat. ▲One Day After Another After the meal, the fellow villager pretended to be deaf and mute and did not mention the passport. The crowd was very anxious and urged him again and again. Finally, he drove them out. When they arrived at the passport office, it was already full of people. They waited for a long time, and the person in charge arrived late. After questioning, they paid 35 gold each and were allowed to pick up their passports at 4 p.m. After the passports were issued, the second step was to buy sleeper tickets for the train. The Chita express train ran once a day, and the slow train ran every other day. They had already missed it that day, so they stayed at the fellow villager's house again. They stayed here for two days. Their hearts were like arrows. At night, the four of them slept in one berth, which was extremely crowded. In the morning, the weather was cold and there was warm water. There was one small washbasin with half a basin of water. The four of them washed their faces and rinsed their mouths in it. The water was as muddy as mud. The hardships of life could not be greater than this. ▲Die as a Communist Ghost There were many overseas Chinese coming and going from the Shanxi villager's residence. They were all in the same predicament. According to them, when the Sino-Soviet conflict broke out over the Middle East Railway the year before last, many Chinese in Russia were arrested by the Latvians and forced to work as laborers. They worked more than ten hours a day, exposed to wind and rain. They were miserable beyond words. They had one meal a day and were hungry all day long. They were often tortured. Those who were seriously injured died. Such cases were not uncommon. They were displaced and worse off than chickens and dogs

Book and Newspaper Introductions: Shanghai People's Food Problem

by Man Yin

Published by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs

(The people are the foundation of the state, and food is the people's heaven.) Although these are old sayings, I think everyone agrees with them. If we look at the history of ancient and modern times, both at home and abroad, we will know that the rise and fall of a country is largely based on whether the people's food is abundant. If the people's food is abundant, the people will live and work in peace and contentment, and society will be stable. There is no country that will not prosper. Otherwise, various disasters, such as bandits and mobs, will arise as a result, social order will be disrupted, and there is no country that will not decline. The most obvious and easily understood example is the recent revolutionary movements that have swept across countries around the world. If we analyze their causes, they are nothing more than the failure to solve the (food) problem of the majority of the people.

Therefore, when we study modern social problems and seek to improve society and alleviate various economic crises, there is no doubt that the people's food problem is a major issue worthy of our careful exploration. We can say that in social problems, whether it is labor problems, population problems, land problems, or even women's problems, all contain the meaning of (food), either because of (food) shortage or (food) inequality. As the saying goes, (Teach people after they are rich.) Guanzi said, (People know honor and disgrace when they have enough food and clothing.) (Sufficient food) is a prerequisite for making the people peaceful, law-abiding, and content... If we encounter years of famine and do not first seek to solve the problem of people's food, but only use morality and law to confine the people's hearts and prevent them from being chaotic, we are putting the cart before the horse, and the result will be like climbing a tree to catch fish, a futile effort.

But let us look at the so-called experts who study social problems today. I don’t know about other countries, but only China is disappointing. It is true that they are writing brilliant theories and shouting nice-sounding slogans. Today, they publish a great work discussing labor-capital disputes, and tomorrow, they give a speech advocating some kind of reformism. However, they have not taken into account the fundamental problem of people's food in social problems. Can this not be said to be an erroneous and contradictory phenomenon?

Since the rise of the revolutionary army, Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Three Principles of the People, with the Principle of People's Livelihood as the main goal of the revolution, the urgent need to solve the problem of people's livelihood has begun to be noticed by the rulers and the majority of the people, reversing the previous mistakes. This is truly gratifying to us. Furthermore, we are particularly pleased that the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs has recently published such a book, rich in material, insightful, combining theory and practice, and promoting both slogans and work, titled (Shanghai People's Food Problem).

The entire book is more than 300 pages, about three hundred thousand words, truly a magnificent sight. For the convenience of introduction, it can be divided into three volumes. The first volume, Essays, is written by various members of the Food Committee of the Bureau of Social Affairs and experts in the study of food and people's food problems at home and abroad. It includes Pan Gongzhan's "Methods for Rectifying People's Food," Huang Kutong's "China's Food Problem," Wu Juenong's "Food Imports and Tax Exemption Problems," "World Rice Production and Supply and Demand," Feng Liutang's "A Study of the Origins of Chinese Grains," Gu Fu's "Private Discussions on Building Charitable Granaries," "Talks on Improving Farming," Zhu Yinong's "Grain Storage and Food Warehouses," Feng Liutang's "A General Overview of Foreign Rice Imports Over the Past Two Hundred Years," "Emergency Measures for Food," Zhu Zixiang's "A General Overview of the Rice Milling Industry in this City," Lu Wenshao's "A General Overview of the Rice Shop Industry in this City," and "A General Overview of the Business Operations of the Rice Shop Industry in this City in 1918," totaling fifteen articles. Now, I will select the most important ones to introduce as follows:

(1) Methods for Rectifying People's Food 146

Without any explanation, we can know the purpose and content of this article from its name. In recent years, the Red Bandits have been rampant, floods and droughts have occurred simultaneously, and natural and man-made disasters have never ceased. The rectification of people's food is imminent. This article is aimed at this point. The full text is divided into five sections: (1) Introduction, an overview of the current situation of insufficient food in China, with more than 2,000 dan of foreign rice imported each year, worth more than 110 million taels of silver, the relationship between agricultural product prices and farmers' lives, a comparison of food prices in the past and present, and bad habits in transportation and sales. The description of the root causes of the current food shortage is quite clear. (2) Discussion on the Issues of Exporting Rice to Suppress Prices and Hoarding. A detailed explanation of the advantages and disadvantages of prohibiting rice exports, the loss of farmers due to the suppression of rice prices, and the method of hoarding rice to save emergency needs. (3) Fundamental Policies, such as establishing a food investigation committee to investigate production and sales, so that (there is enough to store, and enough to prepare for insufficiency), improving rice and wheat production methods to increase harvests, preventing natural disasters and insect pests, and improving agriculture, animal husbandry, and agricultural product manufacturing to increase people's food. These are indeed necessary measures. (4) Stopgap Policies, such as advocating the circulation of food in various provinces to facilitate regulation, prohibiting the planting of opium poppies to avoid consuming farmland, building agricultural product warehouses to alleviate farmers' urgent needs, guiding the increase and decrease of agricultural production, and preventing food waste are also necessary. (5) Matters that urgently need to be carried out to solve the people's food problem in this city, such as advocating the construction of rice wharves, rectifying grain storage, inspecting the quality of rice, registering rice shops, implementing the new peck system, and establishing agricultural experiment fields, etc.... These are all necessary tasks for rectifying the people's food in this city. The opinions in the full text are indeed excellent, the description is concise, and the suggestions for rectifying the people's food in China are based on reason and evidence. It is truly rare.

(2) Food Imports and Tax Exemption Problems 147

This article discusses in detail the great importance of long-term food imports to the national economy. Tax exemption on food will make it impossible for domestic agriculture to recover. If we want to alleviate food shortages and improve production, we should start with the problem of tax exemption. The analysis is thorough and clear. The article is divided into seven sections: introduction, the situation of food imports, tax exemption on spiritual and material food, import and export taxes on rice in various countries, the relationship between tax exemption on food imports and the national economy, why China adopts a tax exemption policy, and conclusion. In the second paragraph, it tells us that the value of food imported by China each year is about 200 million yuan, which is truly alarming. If we calculate a tariff of 10% of the value, we can get 20 million yuan each year. Even if we calculate 2.5% of the value, we can get 5 million yuan. If this amount is used to improve agriculture, the national harvest will inevitably be richer after a few years, but it is uniformly tax-free. How can the loss be estimated? On the other hand, all countries in the world tax food imports. Even countries that are not self-sufficient in food, such as Germany, France, and Japan, have import taxes. The only countries that truly exempt import taxes like China are a small number of countries such as Britain, India, and Annam. The former are industrial countries, and food must be supplied by other countries. The latter are rice-producing countries, and only export food, with no imports, so there is no need to set import taxes. Their situations are not the same as China's. The full text is reasonable and forceful, citing extensively to prove the necessity of collecting taxes on food imports. We have the same feeling after reading it. We hope that the authorities will revise it as soon as possible.

(3) A General Overview of Foreign Rice Imports Over the Past Two Hundred Years 148

The author lists the trend of foreign rice imports into China, which is like climbing a mountain, rising step by step, starting from Emperor Zhenzong of the Song Dynasty to the Yuan, Ming, and Qing Dynasties, with an increase every year. To this day, the losses are in the tens of millions. (The article lists detailed tables, from the Qing Dynasty to the most recent years.) Just imagine, China, which claims to be based on agriculture and produces the most rice in the world, is short of food and relies on foreign sources. The amount is so large every year. Is this problem not worthy of discussion by experts who study social problems and seek to solve the people's livelihood? Although this article does not elaborate on methods to rectify people's food and reverse the leakage, it only (compiles a brief record based on the records in the books, providing considerable material for those who study the problem of people's food.) However, the numbers in these materials are so alarming. The voices of resisting foreign goods have been endless in recent days. If we do not find ways to increase food, which is even more important than foreign goods, and only rely on others, then the harm is a hundred times greater than that of foreign goods. How can we not be afraid?

In addition, the essays in the first volume, such as "China's Food Problem," "Private Discussions on Building Charitable Granaries," "Talks on Improving Rice Cultivation," and "Emergency Measures for Food," either seek to improve farming and increase harvests, or (accumulate the surplus to prepare for insufficiency). In short, they are all fundamental methods for rectifying the people's food problem. Due to space limitations, I cannot introduce them one by one. Readers should read the original book.

The second volume, Food Statistics, lists in detail the amount of various foods imported into Shanghai over the years, the high and low prices, how much is consumed in this city, and how much is left over, to provide resources for research. In China, where everything lacks statistics, we must say that this is a commendable task. Shanghai is the largest city in China, and the amount of food imported and exported is not only related to the people of Shanghai, but also to the people of the whole country. Those who study the food problem in China should not regret that this statistical material is limited to Shanghai alone. That is what should be done.

The third volume is a description of all the practical work carried out by the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs in this city regarding the problem of the people's food in this city. The first section, Food Administration of the Bureau of Social Affairs, recounts the relief and rectification measures taken by the bureau during the food panic in the autumn of 1918 and the spring of 1919, such as registering and evaluating public pecks, handling foreign rice, eliminating malpractices, dredging sources, fair distribution, helping farmers, and preparing storage. The second section, The Work of the Food Committee in the Past Two Years, describes the establishment of the committee and its work achievements, such as the establishment of warehouses, agricultural experiment fields, and rice wharves in the South City, the establishment of rice inspection stations, the prohibition of rice exports, the prevention of rice price increases, the implementation of measures to regulate the people's food, and the organization of price leveling. Other tasks include the drafting of various regulations on rice purchases and sales, and the improvement of all malpractices. The third section, Report on the Handling of Affordable Rice in This City. After 1918, rice prices in this city rose sharply. In view of this, the Food Committee convened committees from all walks of life to organize and handle affordable prices. This section describes the organization process, work overview, and all practical reports of the committee... This volume is rich in materials, concise in description, sufficient for reference for those who study theory, and can also be used as a reference for those who engage in practical work. It is truly a unique kind of writing.

Looking at the entire book, there are many places that deserve special introduction. The most alarming and must be mentioned is that China, which claims to be based on agriculture, relies on foreign countries for its people's food, with tens of millions of dan imported every year and losses of more than tens of millions of taels. There is no doubt that this indicates that China's agriculture is bankrupt. Advocating domestic goods and eliminating leakage is an urgent plan to save the country. Rectifying the people's food problem in domestic goods is an even more urgent plan in the urgent plans. Compatriots, let us quickly seek methods of rectification. Experts who study social problems, please spend more time studying it.

The end of the book includes various simple rules and regulations for establishing and improving organizations that address the people's food problem. Since the laws are good and beautiful, they can be adopted by later generations. The discussion and recording of the rectification of the people's food can be said to be meticulous. It is truly as Mr. Zhang Qun said (see the preface), (We believe that this book is not only helpful for studying the food problem in Shanghai, but also that those who care about the food problem in China should have a copy in hand.) The reporter respectfully introduces it to the readers of this publication. New Book News

▲ An indispensable perspective for those engaged in Nanyang business 149

Mr. Liu Shimu, the editor of this book, has been studying Nanyang for nearly twenty years and regards it as a lifelong career. He has traveled to the inland areas of the British, Dutch, and French colonies in Nanyang three times to conduct on-the-spot investigations. He wrote the book (Japanese Overseas Aggression and Overseas Chinese), with every word a sharp whip and every stroke a deep pain. It is an unprecedented masterpiece introducing the affairs of Nanyang. The content of this book focuses entirely on factual collection, without empty and high-sounding theories. It covers everything about the Japanese policy of advancing south, the steps taken, and their sharp eyes and powerful methods, such as competition in shipping and fishing, the seizure of finance and commerce, the secret observation of the status of Chinese merchants, the operation of small retailers, the threat to the rulers, and the connection with the natives. Even the romantic stories, secret books, and anecdotes are widely collected and incorporated, forming a grand spectacle. If you can have this book in hand, you can not only use it to examine the courage of the Japanese advance south, but also to observe the safety of the status of overseas Chinese, and understand the truth of various businesses in Nanyang. It is truly an outstanding work for studying the Nanyang problem. The price per volume is one yuan. It is sold at the Shanghai and provincial branches of the Commercial Press and in the 28th issue of the Art Garden Weekly.

Art Garden Weekly, a rising star in the publishing industry, has been published for half a year. It can promote its fearless spirit to operate, so it can stand on its own. Its goal is to compile and print a magazine that is true, beautiful, and good, and to create a mental entertainment venue for the masses. Therefore, the content is extremely interesting and valuable, and it is particularly rich in creativity. The binding is artistic and practical. To be fair, this spirit of creating magazines is rare in the modern publishing industry. You will be deeply convinced after reading it. The first volume, issue 28, was published on the 6th of this month. The annual subscription price is one yuan and two corners, and the half-year price is six corners. The address of the company is 732 Qipu Road, Shanghai. It is published every Sunday.

Social News: The Life of a Career Woman in New York (12)

by Lin

The daily life of a woman who earns more than $75 a week, Maureen Sanderson, is as follows:

Maureen is wearing a brightly colored breakfast coat, which is a futuristic style, black with gold trim, and red and purple at the seams, which is very pleasing to the eye. She looked at the clock and it was exactly 9:15. Oh dear, she has an appointment at 10:00 with an administrator at a large company. Maureen works in advertising at that company. Maureen is an important designer at an advertising agency. She is in charge of two important affairs, one of which is mentioned here.

Her work includes advertising design and writing. In addition, she is also a consultant on the company's advertising policies and strategies. She must have the trust and respect of important employees in the company, which is absolutely essential.

Maureen's salary is $100 a week. She studied elsewhere for several years before joining the advertising agency to obtain this superior position. She worked in a department store for two years, specializing in writing advertisements. After that, she worked independently for a year, writing promotional brochures, advertising texts, and various other pieces, doing whatever she could find. Her life was not very stable during this year, because her income was not a fixed amount. Later, she joined this advertising agency and made great progress.

Although she does not have a fixed working hours to keep, she often spends a lot of time at her desk completing her work. When the work is completed, she goes out without much delay.

This morning, she had already thought through the words she would use when she visited. She had already come up with a competitive advertising plan and was determined to win. When she was taking a bath and getting dressed, she regarded it as the best opportunity to use her brain. She first made an outline of the important points, and then wrote a trial copy. She felt that this plan was different from others and would definitely be able to promote the goods. She still had to think carefully about the unfinished part of the plan. Someone often said to Maureen that work does not take a long time and is certainly an easy task. Maureen sometimes replied to them that she had to do many hours of work outside the office. When she was sleeping at night, maybe an idea would pop up in her mind, and she would immediately get out of bed and write down the key points. In the morning, this abstract was sometimes very useful, but sometimes it was very ridiculous.

At 9:30, Maureen left her residence. A few minutes later, she had breakfast at a small shop, where the eggs and milkshakes are very famous. Maureen does not have to worry about how much the things she eats cost, anyway, the things are fair. She does not have to worry about economics either. She lives in a co-op apartment and pays $85 a month for rent. She likes to live alone. She hires a woman to clean up for her, who comes for two hours every day and gets paid 50 cents an hour. Sometimes this assistant woman prepares meals for Maureen and her guests. Maureen often wants to prepare dinner herself. She is very interested in her family and often adds decorative items. She is very interested in modern sculptures, but she cannot always get what she likes.

Maureen can save some money from her salary. She stipulates that she saves $10 a week and uses the money to buy public utility stocks. Sometimes she accumulates cash, but after a period of time, she uses the accumulated money to buy a new chair, a new piece of clothing, or other equally valuable semi-luxury items.

At 10:03, Maureen walked into her office. The person she had an appointment with was already waiting for her. They discussed the advertising plan for an hour and a half. In the end, that person only agreed to half of Maureen's suggestions. He still wanted to think about the entire plan carefully. Maureen just smiled. She thought that if another man had offered this plan to her client, he would have accepted it very readily. In the modern business world, men still have some doubts about women's talents.

Maureen still has to wait. She knows that the things she has encountered before may be encountered again. After a while, that company will adopt the plan she suggested, but will not give her credit. She tried not to think about this in her mind and cheer herself up, thinking that these small things are not worth taking credit for. Maureen hopes that one day she will be able to save enough money to live abroad for a year. Then she will try to write. Maybe she can really write then. She feels emotional about all living things. She treats people with understanding and love. Of course, she has this quality, so that she can describe their lives. In addition, even if the hope in her works cannot be realized, she will not feel unhappy about life.

At 1:00 PM, Maureen had a lunch appointment with Yashu Xinposheng. Xinposheng is a young electrical engineer who is very interested in her. She also likes Yashu and has a good feeling for him. However, he lacks a kind of magic that others have, a magic of surprise and attraction. Yashu wants her to marry him. Maureen can't think of a reason why not to marry him. He is handsome, successful, and reliable. Maureen's heart is full of romance. Once she falls in love, she wants to take it all away. She wants to get married if she feels that she can get extraordinary happiness from it. She does not need children now, although she knows that she can love her own son. (To be continued)

The City Chamber of Commerce Again Petitions for the Reduction of Shanxi Coal Freight Rates 150

Over 100,000 Tons of Coal Stockpiled in Northern Shanxi

Urgent Hope for Prompt Enactment of Fee Reduction Measures

Yesterday, the City Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Railways in Nanjing, requesting a reduction in freight rates to facilitate the transportation of stockpiled coal from northern Shanxi. The original telegram read: "To the esteemed Ministry of Railways: In May of this year, regarding the petition for a reduction in Shanxi coal freight rates, we received your ministry's reply, via telegram, on the 18th of the same month, stating that the current increase in freight rates across various routes was a measure taken out of necessity, and that it was difficult to make immediate changes at this time. After relaying this information to the Kouquan Station Coal Industry Joint Association, we subsequently received a letter from the same association on August 24th, stating that the association had simultaneously submitted a memorial to your ministry, which was given the reference number 業字第八八九, indicating that the railway transportation of coal was of utmost importance to the people's livelihood and national revenue, and that a comprehensive investigation of transportation conditions across various routes was currently underway, with a plan to devise appropriate measures after ascertaining the actual situation. Two months have passed, but we have not received any further instructions. Meanwhile, the Shanxi Provincial Mining Bureau and the Baojin Company have stockpiled over 100,000 tons of coal, and the mines are reducing production by only 200 tons per day in order to maintain the livelihood of the miners, a situation that is becoming increasingly precarious. We have already sent a clever telegram to your ministry, requesting that the reduction of Shanxi coal freight rates on the Ping-Sui Railway be implemented as soon as possible, and we are providing a copy of the telegram for your coordinated appeal. Furthermore, upon examining Industrial Bulletin No. 30, we found an article containing a letter from the Ministry of Industry to the China Mining Association, which quoted a reply from your ministry to the Ministry of Industry stating that the Jiaoji, Ping-Sui, and other railways had special circumstances regarding coal transportation, and that your ministry had already established separate measures to reduce freight rates in order to maintain the coal industry. Therefore, the need to reduce Shanxi coal freight rates has been repeatedly emphasized by the association and the Ministry of Industry, and your ministry is already aware of this and has agreed to make revisions. However, much time has passed, and no implementation has occurred, and the coal industry still has no hope of recovery. Based on the aforementioned situation, we respectfully submit this telegram to your ministry for your review and approval, requesting that you promptly enact measures to reduce Shanxi coal freight rates on the Ping-Sui Railway, in order to alleviate the burden on mine operators, expand the market for domestic coal, stem losses, and enrich the people's livelihood. This one action is of the utmost urgency. Yours respectfully, the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce."

Guizhou Representatives Host the Road Association 151

Hua Laifeng and Lü Huimin, representatives of the Guizhou Provincial Government, who were in Shanghai to participate in the Road and City Exhibition, hosted a reception last night at the Xin Xin Restaurant for representatives of the Road Association. Over twenty people attended, including Cao Yunxiang and Wu Shan. Mr. Hua delivered a response speech. Mr. Lü Huimin, the Guizhou representative, brought a large number of exhibits, representing a journey of over twenty days from Guizhou. The exhibits demonstrate the province's spirit of construction in recent years, as well as the excellence of its products. The Road and City Exhibition has established a Guizhou Pavilion specifically for this purpose, which can be considered second to none.

Research Committee on Sino-Japanese Agreed Tariff Rate to Convene Tomorrow 152

Following its establishment and registration with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Research Committee on Sino-Japanese Agreed Tariff Rate will convene its first committee meeting at the National Products Preservation Association at Nine Acres Land on the 11th of this month to discuss all aspects of its operations. All committee members have been notified.

Temporary Market at the Festival of the Three Officials 153

Yesterday was the 27th day of the seventh lunar month, traditionally known as the Festival of the Three Officials. Adhering to custom, merchants and common people set up stalls to conduct business outside the Great South Gate of the South City, on Great Buddha Factory Road, Fushan Hall Street, and in the Lujiabang area. All kinds of household goods were readily available. Residents in the vicinity flocked to make purchases, creating a crowded scene akin to that on the Shanyin Road. Chief Jin of the First District, Third Precinct, dispatched many police officers to patrol the area in shifts from morning to night. This situation was, in effect, a temporary national products market.

The Busy Shi Zhen at Bao He Tang 154

Since August 1st, the Hongkou Branch of Bao He Tang on North Sichuan Road has added a free clinic department, hiring many renowned physicians. They take turns providing free medical consultations daily from 7:00 AM to 5:00 PM. As a result, there is a constant stream of patients seeking treatment, and the physicians are exceptionally busy. Mr. Huang Zhihe arrives at the clinic every morning at 7:00 AM and treats dozens of patients. Mr. Huang is a distinguished student of the late renowned physician Fan Xiangling, possessing exceptional medical skills and extensive experience, and is highly respected by the community.
